(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/generators' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
	FUNCTION_BLOCK CLK_Prg
VAR_INPUT
	PT : TIME := t#10ms;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	Q : BOOL := 0;
END_VAR
VAR
	init : BOOL := FALSE;
	last : TIME;
	tx: TIME;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.2	17 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

clk_prg uses the internal sps time to generate a clock with programmable period time.
the period time is defined for 10ms .. 65s
the first cycle after start is a clk pulse and then depending on the programmed period time a delay.
every pulse is only valid for one cycle.
the accuracy of clk_prg is depending on the accuracy of the system clock.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* read system time *)
tx := DWORD_TO_TIME(T_PLC_MS());

(* initialize on startup *)
IF NOT init THEN
	init := TRUE;
	last := tx - pt;
END_IF;

(* generate output pulse when next_pulse is reached *)
IF tx - last >= pt THEN
	Q := TRUE;
	last := tx;
ELSE
	Q := FALSE;
END_IF;


(* revision hiostory

hm 25 feb 2007	rev 1.1
	rewritten code for higher performance
	pt can now be changed during runtime

hm	17. sep 2007	rev 1.2
	replaced time() with t_plc_ms() for compatibility reasons

*)
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/generators' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK CLK_Pulse
VAR_INPUT
	PT : TIME := t#10ms;
	N : INT := 0;
	rst : BOOL := 0;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	Q : BOOL := 0;
	cnt : INT := 0;
	run : BOOL := 0;
END_VAR
VAR
	pti : TIME := t#0ms;
	next_pulse: TIME := T#0s;
	overflow: BOOL := FALSE;
	tx: TIME;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	17 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

clk_pulse uses the internal sps time to generate a clock with programmable period time.
the period time is defined for 10ms .. 65s.
pulse generation is continuous if N = 0 and for n pulses otherwise.
if the period time is set to less then 10ms the min clock perid is 10ms.
the first cycle after start is a clk pulse and then depending on the programmed period time a delay.
every pulse is only valid for one cycle so that a edge trigger is not necessary
clk_prg depending on the accuracy of the system clock.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* read system *)
tx := DWORD_TO_TIME(T_PLC_MS());


IF rst THEN
	run := FALSE;
	pti := t#0ms;
	next_pulse := t#0ms;
	overflow := FALSE;
	Q := FALSE;
	cnt := 0;
ELSIF cnt <= N OR N = 0 THEN
	IF NOT run THEN
		next_pulse := tx;
		run := TRUE;
		IF pt < T#10ms THEN PTI := T#10ms; ELSE pti := pt; END_IF;
	END_IF;
	IF tx >= next_pulse AND NOT overflow AND (cnt < N OR N = 0) THEN
		Q := TRUE;
		cnt := cnt + 1;
		IF next_pulse + pti < next_pulse THEN
			overflow := TRUE;
		END_IF;
		next_pulse := next_pulse + pti;
	ELSE
		Q := FALSE;
		IF cnt = N THEN run := FALSE; END_IF
		IF tx <= next_pulse THEN overflow := FALSE; END_IF;
	END_IF;
END_IF

(* revision history
hm		4. aug 2006		rev 1.0
	original version

hm		17. sep 2007	rev 1.1
	replaced time() with T_PLC_S() fr compatblity reasons

*)
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/generators' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK D_Trig
VAR_INPUT
	in : DWORD;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	Q : BOOL;
	X : DWORD;
END_VAR
VAR
	last_in : DWORD;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	4 Sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this block is similar to the IEC Standard R_trig and F_trig but it monitors a DWORD, WORD or Byte Variable instead and generated an Output Pulse for one cycle only when the input has changed.
an additional output x (Dword) will state the chage of the input.
Example: the input has chaged from 0001 to 0010 then the output x will be 2.

*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
IF (in XOR last_in) <> 0 THEN
	Q := TRUE;
	X := in - last_in;
	last_in := in;
ELSE
	Q := FALSE;
END_IF;


(* revision history

hm 4.09.2007	rev 1.0
	original version released

*)
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/generators' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK gen_bit
VAR_INPUT
	in0 : DWORD;
	in1 : DWORD;
	in2 : DWORD;
	in3 : DWORD;
	clk : BOOL := 0;
	steps : INT;
	rep : INT := 0;
	rst : BOOL := 0;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	Q0 :BOOL := 0;
	Q1 :BOOL := 0;
	Q2 :BOOL := 0;
	Q3 :BOOL := 0;
	cnt : INT := 0;
	run : BOOL := 0;
END_VAR
VAR
	r0: DWORD;
	r1: DWORD;
	r2: DWORD;
	r3: DWORD;
	rx : INT := 1;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	4 aug 2006
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

gen_bit is 4 bit sequencial pattern generator with 4 DWORD inputs and 4 serial outputs.
with the first clock pulse after a reset or after power on, bit 0 of the input DWORDS IN is present on the Outputs Q and the next clock cycle shifts to Bit 1 and so on.
the input steps defines how many bits of the input dwords will be shifted to the outputs. the sequence can be repetive when rep = 0 or any amount of repetitions can be defined with input rep.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* check if number of runs is finished or rep = 0 which means continuous *)

IF clk AND NOT rst THEN
	IF (rep = 0) OR (rx <= rep) THEN run := TRUE; ELSE run := FALSE; END_IF;
	IF run THEN
		(* check for step counter reached and reset to 0 if cnt = steps *)
		IF cnt = steps THEN
			cnt := 0;
		END_IF;

		(* when cnt = 0 then reload the inputs into the registers *)
		IF cnt = 0 THEN
			r0 := in0;
			r1 := in1;
			r2 := in2;
			r3 := in3;
		END_IF;

		(* when cnt < steps, shift the lowest bits to the outputs *)
		IF (cnt < steps) THEN
			Q0 := r0.0;
			Q1 := r1.0;
			Q2 := r2.0;
			Q3 := r3.0;
			r0 := SHR(r0,1);
			r1 := SHR(r1,1);
			r2 := SHR(r2,1);
			r3 := SHR(r3,1);
		END_IF;

		(* increment the step counter *)
		cnt := cnt +1;
		IF (cnt = steps) AND (rep <> 0) THEN rx := rx +1; END_IF;
		IF (rx > rep) AND (rep <> 0) THEN run := FALSE; END_IF;
	END_IF;
ELSE
	IF rst THEN
		Q0 := FALSE;
		Q1 := FALSE;
		Q2 := FALSE;
		Q3 := FALSE;
		r0 := 0;
		r1 := 0;
		r2 := 0;
		r3 := 0;
		cnt := 0;
		run := FALSE;
		rx := 1;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/generators' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK gen_SQ
VAR_INPUT
	PT : TIME := T#0ms;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	Q : BOOL := 0;
END_VAR
VAR
	pti : TIME := t#0ms;
	run: BOOL := FALSE;
	next_edge: TIME := t#0ms;
	overflow: BOOL := 0;
	tx: TIME;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	17 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

gen_sq generates square wave signal with programmable period time.
the period time is defined for 10ms .. 65s
if the period time is set to less then 10ms the min perid is 10ms.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* read system time *)
tx := DWORD_TO_TIME(T_PLC_MS());

IF NOT run THEN
	next_edge := Tx;
	run := TRUE;
	IF pt < T#10ms THEN PTI := T#5ms; ELSE pti := pt / 2; END_IF;
END_IF;
IF (Tx >= next_edge) AND NOT overflow THEN
	Q := NOT Q;
	IF next_edge + pti < next_edge THEN
		(* time() will overflow every 50 days *)
		overflow := TRUE;
	END_IF;
	next_edge := next_edge + pti;
ELSE
	(* wait till time() has an overflow and reset overflow *)
	IF Tx <= next_edge THEN overflow := FALSE; END_IF;
END_IF;

(* revision history
hm	4. aug 2006		rev 1.0
	original version

hm	17. sep 2007	rev 1.1
	replaced time() with T_PLC_MS() for compatibility reasons

*)




END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/generators' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK sequence_4
VAR_INPUT
	in0 : BOOL := TRUE;
	in1 : BOOL := TRUE;
	in2 : BOOL := TRUE;
	in3 : BOOL := TRUE;
	start : BOOL;
	rst : BOOL;
	wait0 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay0 : TIME := t#0s;
	wait1 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay1 : TIME := t#0s;
	wait2 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay2 : TIME := t#0s;
	wait3 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay3 : TIME := t#0s;
END_VAR
VAR_INPUT CONSTANT
	stop_on_error : BOOL := FALSE;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	Q0 : BOOL;
	Q1 : BOOL;
	Q2 : BOOL;
	Q3 : BOOL;
	any : BOOL;
	run: BOOL;
	step : INT := -1;
	status : BYTE := 0;
END_VAR
VAR
	last : TIME;
	edge : BOOL;
	tx: TIME;
	init: BOOL;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.4	17 sep 2007
programmer 	oscat
tested by	hans

sequence_4 enables run when a low to high transition is present on start.
a low to high transition on start will restart the sequencer at any time while a rst will hold the sequencer in reset while true.
after run is enabled with a rising edge on start the sequencer waits for wait0 on in0 to enable q0 which stays on for delay0.
the next cycle starts with wait1, continues with delay 1 and so on...
if an edge is not detected during the wait period, the sequencer will then display the error number on the status output.
the status numbers 1..4 are errors in step 0..3.
after the last step that sets q3, the sequencer leaves q3 on for delay3 and then resets to the initial state.
a step output will indicate the current step of the sequencer and will also be present with a fault condition.
after the first output is turened on the sequencer switches from q0 to q1 and so on, at any time there is only one output enabled.
if an input signal is not detected during a wait period, the sequencer will display the error number ( 1 for in0, 2 for in1 .... ).
when an error is present and the config variable stop_on_error is set then the sequencer will stop. otherwise it will continue.
The status output will also display 110 for waiting and 111 for sequence running.
*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* read sps timer *)
tx := DWORD_TO_TIME(T_PLC_MS());

(* initialize on startup *)
IF NOT init THEN
	last := tx;
	init := TRUE;
	status := 110;
END_IF;

(* asynchronous reset *)
IF rst THEN
	step := -1;
	Q0 := 0;
	Q1 := 0;
	Q2 := 0;
	Q3 := 0;
	status := 110;
	run := 0;

(* edge on start input restarts the sequencer *)
ELSIF start AND NOT edge THEN
	step := 0;
	last := tx;
	status := 111;
	Q0 := 0;
	Q1 := 0;
	Q2 := 0;
	Q3 := 0;
	run := 1;
END_IF;
edge := start;

(* check if stop on status is necessary *)
IF status > 0 AND status < 100 AND stop_on_error THEN RETURN; END_IF;

(* sequence is running *)
IF run AND step = 0 THEN
	IF NOT q0 AND in0 AND tx - last <= wait0 THEN
		Q0 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q0 AND tx - last > wait0 THEN
		status := 1;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q0 AND tx - last >= delay0 THEN
		step := 1;
		last := tx;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
IF run AND step = 1 THEN
	IF NOT q1 AND in1 AND tx - last <= wait1 THEN
		Q0 := FALSE;
		Q1 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q1 AND Tx - last > wait1 THEN
		status := 2;
		q0 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q1 AND tx - last >= delay1 THEN
		step := 2;
		last := tx;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
IF run AND step = 2 THEN
	IF NOT q2 AND in2 AND tx - last <= wait2 THEN
		Q1 := FALSE;
		Q2 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q2 AND Tx - last > wait2 THEN
		status := 3;
		q1 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q2 AND tx - last >= delay2 THEN
		step := 3;
		last := tx;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
IF run AND step = 3 THEN
	IF NOT q3 AND in3 AND tx - last <= wait3 THEN
		Q2 := FALSE;
		Q3 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q3 AND Tx - last > wait3 THEN
		status := 4;
		q2 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q3 AND tx - last >= delay3 THEN
		step := -1;
		q3 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
		status := 110;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
any := q0 OR q1 OR q2 OR q3;

(*
hm 1.10.06		rev 1.1
	corrected delay logic to be after event and not before
	added any output

hm 1.12.06		rev 1.2
	corrected failure in sequence logic.
	added init at startup to prevent from initial error after start.

hm 17.1.2007		rev 1.3
	changed output fault to status for better compatibility with other modules (ESR).
	added stop on error functionality and setup variable
	default for inputs in0..3 is true.
	renamed variable state to step

hm	17.sep 2007		rev 1.4
	replaced time() with T_PLC_MS() for compatibility reasons

*)
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/generators' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK sequence_8
VAR_INPUT
	in0 : BOOL := TRUE;
	in1 : BOOL := TRUE;
	in2 : BOOL := TRUE;
	in3 : BOOL := TRUE;
	in4 : BOOL := TRUE;
	in5 : BOOL := TRUE;
	in6 : BOOL := TRUE;
	in7 : BOOL := TRUE;
	start : BOOL;
	rst : BOOL;
	wait0 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay0 : TIME := t#0s;
	wait1 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay1 : TIME := t#0s;
	wait2 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay2 : TIME := t#0s;
	wait3 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay3 : TIME := t#0s;
	wait4 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay4 : TIME := t#0s;
	wait5 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay5 : TIME := t#0s;
	wait6 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay6 : TIME := t#0s;
	wait7 : TIME := t#0s;
	delay7 : TIME := t#0s;
END_VAR
VAR_INPUT CONSTANT
	stop_on_error : BOOL := FALSE;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	Q0 : BOOL;
	Q1 : BOOL;
	Q2 : BOOL;
	Q3 : BOOL;
	Q4 : BOOL;
	Q5 : BOOL;
	Q6 : BOOL;
	Q7 : BOOL;
	any : BOOL;
	run: BOOL;
	step : INT := -1;
	status : BYTE;
END_VAR
VAR
	last : TIME;
	edge : BOOL;
	tx: TIME;
	init: BOOL;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.4	17 sep 2007
programmer 	oscat
tested by		hans

sequence_8 enables run when a low to high transition is present on start.
a low to high transition on start will restart the sequencer at any time while a rst will hold the sequencer in reset while true.
after run is enabled with a rising edge on start the sequencer waits for wait0 on in0 to enable q0 which stays on for delay0.
the next cycle starts with wait1, continues with delay 1 and so on...
if an edge is not detected during the wait period, the sequencer will then display the error number on the status output.
The status numbers are 1 .. 8 for erros in step 0..7.
after the last step that sets q7, the sequencer leaves q7 on for delay7 and then resets to the initial state.
a step output will indicate the current step of the sequencer and will also be present with a fault condition.
after the first output is turened on the sequencer switches from q0 to q1 and so on, at any time there is only one output enabled.
if an input signal is not detected during a wait period, the sequencer will display the error number ( 1 for in0, 2 for in1 .... ).
when an error is present and the config variable stop_on_error is set then the sequencer will stop. otherwise it will continue.
The status output will also display 110 for waiting and 111 sequece running.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* read sps timer *)
tx := DWORD_TO_TIME(T_PLC_MS());

(* initialize on startup *)
IF NOT init THEN
	last := tx;
	init := TRUE;
	status := 110;
END_IF;

(* asynchronous reset *)
IF rst THEN
	step := -1;
	Q0 := 0;
	Q1 := 0;
	Q2 := 0;
	Q3 := 0;
	Q4 := 0;
	Q5 := 0;
	Q6 := 0;
	Q7 := 0;
	status := 110;
	run := 0;

(* edge on start input restarts the sequencer *)
ELSIF start AND NOT edge THEN
	step := 0;
	last := tx;
	status := 111;
	Q0 := 0;
	Q1 := 0;
	Q2 := 0;
	Q3 := 0;
	Q4 := 0;
	Q5 := 0;
	Q6 := 0;
	Q7 := 0;
	run := 1;
END_IF;
edge := start;

(* check if stop on error is necessary *)
IF status > 0 AND status < 100 AND stop_on_error THEN RETURN; END_IF;

(* sequence is running *)
IF run AND step = 0 THEN
	IF NOT q0 AND in0 AND tx - last <= wait0 THEN
		Q0 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q0 AND tx - last > wait0 THEN
		status := 1;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q0 AND tx - last >= delay0 THEN
		step := 1;
		last := tx;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
IF run AND step = 1 THEN
	IF NOT q1 AND in1 AND tx - last <= wait1 THEN
		Q0 := FALSE;
		Q1 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q1 AND Tx - last > wait1 THEN
		status := 2;
		q0 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q1 AND tx - last >= delay1 THEN
		step := 2;
		last := tx;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
IF run AND step = 2 THEN
	IF NOT q2 AND in2 AND tx - last <= wait2 THEN
		Q1 := FALSE;
		Q2 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q2 AND Tx - last > wait2 THEN
		status := 3;
		q1 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q2 AND tx - last >= delay2 THEN
		step := 3;
		last := tx;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
IF run AND step = 3 THEN
	IF NOT q3 AND in3 AND tx - last <= wait3 THEN
		Q2 := FALSE;
		Q3 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q3 AND Tx - last > wait3 THEN
		status := 4;
		q2 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q3 AND tx - last >= delay3 THEN
		step := 4;
		last := tx;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
IF run AND step = 4 THEN
	IF NOT q4 AND in4 AND tx - last <= wait4 THEN
		Q3 := FALSE;
		Q4 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q4 AND Tx - last > wait4 THEN
		status := 5;
		q3 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q4 AND tx - last >= delay4 THEN
		step := 5;
		last := tx;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
IF run AND step = 5 THEN
	IF NOT q5 AND in5 AND tx - last <= wait5 THEN
		Q4 := FALSE;
		Q5 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q5 AND Tx - last > wait5 THEN
		status := 6;
		q4 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q5 AND tx - last >= delay5 THEN
		step := 6;
		last := tx;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
IF run AND step = 6 THEN
	IF NOT q6 AND in6 AND tx - last <= wait6 THEN
		Q5 := FALSE;
		Q6 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q6 AND Tx - last > wait6 THEN
		status := 7;
		q5 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q6 AND tx - last >= delay6 THEN
		step := 7;
		last := tx;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
IF run AND step = 7 THEN
	IF NOT q7 AND in7 AND tx - last <= wait7 THEN
		Q6 := FALSE;
		Q7 := TRUE;
		last := tx;
	ELSIF NOT q7 AND Tx - last > wait7 THEN
		status := 8;
		q6 := FALSE;
		run := FALSE;
	ELSIF q7 AND tx - last >= delay7 THEN
		step := -1;
		Q7 := FALSE;
		Run := FALSE;
		status := 110;
	END_IF;
END_IF;
any := q0 OR q1 OR q2 OR q3 OR q4 OR q5 OR q6 OR q7;

(*
hm 1.10.06		rev 1.1
	corrected delay logic to be after event and not before
	added any output

hm 1.12.06		rev 1.2
	corrected failure in sequence logic.
	added init at startup to prevent from initial statuss after start.

hm 17.1.2007		rev 1.3
	changed output fault to status for better compatibility with other modules (ESR)
	added stop on error functionality and setup variable
	default for inputs in0..7 is true.
	renames variable state to step

hm	17.sep 2007		rev 1.4
	replaced time() with T_PLC_MS() for compatibility reasons

*)
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK

FUNCTION_BLOCK TP_R
VAR_INPUT
	in : BOOL;
	PT : TIME;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	Q : BOOL := 0;
	ET : TIME := t#0ms;
END_VAR
VAR
	edge : BOOL := FALSE;
	start : TIME := t#0ms;
	tx: TIME;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	17 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

retriggerable edge triggered pulse similar to TP but with a retrigger function
if the pt input is 0 then output is always low.
*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* read system_time *)
tx := DWORD_TO_TIME(T_PLC_MS());

(* rising edge trigger *)
IF in AND NOT edge THEN
	start := Tx;
	IF pt > t#0ms THEN Q := TRUE; END_IF;
END_IF;
edge := in;
IF q THEN
	et := Tx - start;
	IF et >= PT THEN
		Q := FALSE;
		et := t#0ms;
	END_IF;
END_IF;

	original version

	replaced time() with T_PLC_MS() for compatibility reasons

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/memory' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK FIFO_16
VAR_INPUT
	Din : DWORD;
	WR : BOOL;
	E : BOOL;
	RST : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	Dout : DWORD := 0;
	empty : BOOL := TRUE;
	full : BOOL := FALSE;
END_VAR
VAR
	fifo : ARRAY[0..15] OF DWORD;
	NW : INT := 0;
	NR : INT := 0;
	top : INT := 15;
END_VAR

(*
	version 1.0	4 aug 2006
	programmer 	hugo
	tested by		tobias

16 Dword FIFO memory
*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
IF rst THEN
	(* asynchronous reset for the fifo *)
	NW := 0;
	NR := 0;
	Dout := 0;
	empty := TRUE;
	full := FALSE;
ELSIF WR AND E AND NOT full THEN
	(* write action *)
	fifo[NW] := Din;
	IF NW = top THEN NW := 0; ELSE NW := NW + 1; END_IF
	IF NW = NR THEN full := TRUE; END_IF
	empty := FALSE;
ELSIF NOT WR AND E AND NOT empty THEN
	(* read from stack *)
	Dout := fifo[NR];
	IF NR = top THEN NR := 0; ELSE NR := NR + 1; END_IF;
	IF NR = NW THEN empty := TRUE; END_IF;
	full := FALSE;
END_IF;

END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/memory' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK STACK_16
VAR_INPUT
	Din : DWORD;
	RW : BOOL;
	E : BOOL;
	RST : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	Dout : DWORD := 0;
	empty : BOOL := TRUE;
	full : BOOL := FALSE;
END_VAR
VAR
	Stack : ARRAY[0..15] OF DWORD;
	N : INT := -1;
	top : INT := 15;
END_VAR

(*
	version 1.0	4 aug 2006
	programmer 	hugo
	tested by		tobias

16 Dword STACK memory
*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
IF rst THEN
	(* asynchronous reset for the fifo *)
	N := -1;
	Dout := 0;
	empty := TRUE;
	full := FALSE;
ELSIF RW AND E AND NOT full THEN
	(* write action *)
	N := N + 1;
	IF N = top THEN full := TRUE; END_IF;
	empty := FALSE;
	stack[N] := Din;
ELSIF NOT RW AND E AND NOT empty THEN
	(* read from stack *)
	Dout := stack[N];
	N := N -1;
	IF N < 0 THEN empty := TRUE; END_IF;
	full := FALSE;
END_IF;

END_FUNCTION_BLOCK

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/Others' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION CRC_CHECK : BOOL
VAR_INPUT
	pt : POINTER TO ARRAY[0..32000] OF BYTE;
	size : INT;
END_VAR
VAR_INPUT CONSTANT
	Polynom_L : DWORD;
	Polynom_32 : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR
	temp: DWORD;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	9 jun 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

CRC_CHECK checks a block of data for a crc checksum and returns true is the checksum is 0 and therfore a error free data transmission.
the CRC Polynom is specified with the config variable Polynom_L which holds the lowest 32 bits of the polynom and Polynom_33 which holds bit 33 of the Polynom.
A Polynom x4 + X + 1 is represented by 10011.
The input data is an array of byte of any size, the function is called by CRC_CHECK(ADR(array),SIZEOF(array)).

*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
temp := CRC_GEN(pt, size, polynom_L, polynom_32);
IF temp = 0 THEN CRC_CHECK := TRUE; ELSE CRC_CHECK := FALSE; END_IF;

(* typical crc polynoms

CRC-4-ITU 			x4 + x + 1 					(ITU G.704, p. 12) 	0x3 or 0xC (0x9)
CRC-5-ITU 			x5 + x4 + x2 + 1 			(ITU G.704, p. 9) 	0x15 or 0x15 (0x0B)
CRC-5-USB 			x5 + x2 + 1 				(use: USB token packets) 	0x05 or 0x14 (0x9)
CRC-6-ITU 			x6 + x + 1 					(ITU G.704, p. 3) 	0x03 or 0x30 (0x21)
CRC-7 				x7 + x3 + 1 				(use: telecom systems, MMC) 	0x09 or 0x48 (0x11)
CRC-8-ATM 			x8 + x2 + x + 1 				(use: ATM HEC) 	0x07 or 0xE0 (0xC1)
CRC-8-CCITT 		x8 + x7 + x3 + x2 + 1 		(use: 1-Wire bus) 	0x8D or 0xB1 (0x63)
CRC-8-Dallas/Maxim 	x8 + x5 + x4 + 1 			(use: 1-Wire bus) 	0x31 or 0x8C (0x19)
CRC-8 				x8 + x7 + x6 + x4 + x2 + 1 	0xD5 or 0xAB (0x57)
CRC-8-SAE J1850 	x8 + x4 + x3 + x2 + 1 		0x1D or 0xB8
CRC-10 				x10 + x9 + x5 + x4 + x + 1 	0x233 or 0x331 (0x263)
CRC-12 				x12 + x11 + x3 + x2 + x + 1 (use: telecom systems) 	0x80F or 0xF01 (0xE03)
CRC-15-CAN 			x15 + x14 + x10 + x8 + x7 + x4 + x3 + 1 	0x4599 or 0x4CD1 (0x19A3)
CRC-16-Fletcher 	Not a CRC; see Fletcher's checksum 	Used in Adler-32 A & B CRCs
CRC-16-CCITT 	x16 + x12 + x5 + 1 (XMODEM,X.25, V.41, Bluetooth, PPP, IrDA; known as "CRC-CCITT") 	0x1021 or 0x8408 (0x0811)
CRC-16-IBM 	x16 + x15 + x2 + 1 (USB, many others; also known as "CRC-16") 	0x8005 or 0xA001 (0x4003)
CRC-24-Radix-64 	x24 + x23 + x18 + x17 + x14 + x11 + x10 + x7 + x6 + x5 + x4 + x3 + x + 1 	0x864CFB or 0xDF3261 (0xBE64C3)
CRC-32-Adler 	Not a CRC; see Adler-32 	See Adler-32
CRC-32-MPEG2 	x32 + x26 + x23 + x22 + x16 + x12 + x11 + x10 + x8 + x7 + x5 + x4 + x2 + x + 1 	0x04C11DB7 or 0xEDB88320 (0xDB710641) Also used in IEEE 802.3
CRC-32-IEEE 802.3 	x32 + x26 + x23 + x22 + x16 + x12 + x11 + x10 + x8 + x7 + x5 + x4 + x2 + x + 1 (V.42) 	0x04C11DB7 or 0xEDB88320 (0xDB710641)
CRC-32C (Castagnoli) 	x32 + x28 + x27 + x26 + x25 + x23 + x22 + x20 + x19 + x18 + x14 + x13 + x11 + x10 + x9 + x8 + x6 + 1 	0x1EDC6F41 or 0x82F63B78 (0x05EC76F1)
CRC-64-ISO 	x64 + x4 + x3 + x + 1 (use: ISO 3309) 	0x000000000000001B or 0xD800000000000000 (0xB000000000000001)
CRC-64-ECMA-182 	x64 + x62 + x57 + x55 + x54 + x53 + x52 + x47 + x46 + x45 + x40 + x39 + x38 + x37 + x35 + x33 + x32 + x31 + x29 + x27 + x24 + x23 + x22 + x21 + x19 + x17 + x13 + x12 + x10 + x9 + x7 + x4 + x + 1
(as described in ECMA-182 p.63) 	0x42F0E1EBA9EA3693 or 0xC96C5795D7870F42 (0x92D8AF2BAF0E1E85)

*)

(* revision history

hm		9.6.2007	rev 1.0		original version 

*)
END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/Others' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION CRC_GEN : DWORD

VAR_INPUT
	pt : POINTER TO ARRAY[0..32000] OF BYTE;
	size : INT;
END_VAR
VAR_INPUT CONSTANT
	Polynom_L : DWORD;
	Polynom_32 : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR
	polynom : DWORD;
	p_length : INT;
	B1, B2, B3, B4, BS : BYTE;
	data : DWORD;
	count : BYTE;
	temp : BOOL;
	step: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	11 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

CRC_GEN generates a CRC checksum from a block of data and returns  the checksum in a DWORD to be connected to the data for transmission.
the CRC Polynom is specified with the config variable Polynom_L which holds the lowest 32 bits of the polynom and Polynom_33 which holds bit 33 of the Polynom.
A Polynom x4 + X + 1 is represented by 10011.
The input data is an array of byte of any size, the function is called by CRC_GEN(ADR(array),SIZEOF(array)).

*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* check for polynom length and calculate p_length polynom will be aligned to high side of word*)
polynom := polynom_L;
IF polynom_32 = 1 THEN
	p_length := 33;
ELSE;
	p_length := 32;
	WHILE Polynom.31 = 0 AND p_length > 0 DO
		p_length := p_length - 1;
		Polynom := SHL(polynom,1);
	END_WHILE;
	Polynom := SHL(polynom,1);
END_IF;

(* load first 4 data bytes for crc calculation *)
B1 := pt^[0];
IF size > 1 THEN B2 := pt^[1]; ELSE B2 := 0; END_IF;
IF size > 2 THEN B3 := pt^[2]; ELSE B3 := 0; END_IF;
IF size > 3 THEN B4 := pt^[3]; ELSE B4 := 0; END_IF;
IF size > 4 THEN BS := pt^[4]; ELSE BS := 0; END_IF;
data := DWord_of_Byte(B4,B3,B2,B1);

WHILE step < size DO
	temp := data.31;
	data := SHL(data,1);
	data.0 := BS.7;
	bs := SHL(bs,1);
	count := count + 1;
	IF count = 8 THEN
		step := step + 1;
		count := 0;
		IF step + 4 < size THEN bs := pt^[step+ 4]; END_IF;
	END_IF;
	(* check highest bit if true then xor polynom *)
	IF temp = TRUE THEN
		data := data XOR polynom;
	END_IF;
END_WHILE;

(* align crc checksum to left of dword *)
CRC_GEN := SHR(data,32 - p_length +1);

(* typical crc polynoms

CRC-4-ITU 			x4 + x + 1 					(ITU G.704, p. 12) 	0x3 or 0xC (0x9)
CRC-5-ITU 			x5 + x4 + x2 + 1 			(ITU G.704, p. 9) 	0x15 or 0x15 (0x0B) Bluetooth
CRC-5-USB 			x5 + x2 + 1 				(use: USB token packets) 	0x05 or 0x14 (0x9)
CRC-6-ITU 			x6 + x + 1 					(ITU G.704, p. 3) 	0x03 or 0x30 (0x21)
CRC-7 				x7 + x3 + 1 				(use: telecom systems, MMC) 	0x09 or 0x48 (0x11)
CRC-8-ATM 			x8 + x2 + x + 1 				(use: ATM HEC) 	0x07 or 0xE0 (0xC1)
CRC-8-CCITT 		x8 + x7 + x3 + x2 + 1 		(use: 1-Wire bus) 	0x8D or 0xB1 (0x63)
CRC-8-Dallas/Maxim 	x8 + x5 + x4 + 1 			(use: 1-Wire bus) 	0x31 or 0x8C (0x19)
CRC-8 				x8 + x7 + x6 + x4 + x2 + 1 	0xD5 or 0xAB (0x57)
CRC-8-SAE J1850 	x8 + x4 + x3 + x2 + 1 		0x1D or 0xB8
CRC-10 				x10 + x9 + x5 + x4 + x + 1 	0x233 or 0x331 (0x263)
CRC-12 				x12 + x11 + x3 + x2 + x + 1 (use: telecom systems) 	0x80F or 0xF01 (0xE03)
CRC-15-CAN 			x15 + x14 + x10 + x8 + x7 + x4 + x3 + 1 	0x4599 or 0x4CD1 (0x19A3)
CRC-16-Fletcher 	Not a CRC; see Fletcher's checksum 	Used in Adler-32 A & B CRCs
CRC-16-CCITT 	x16 + x12 + x5 + 1 (XMODEM,X.25, V.41, Bluetooth, PPP, IrDA; known as "CRC-CCITT") 	0x1021 or 0x8408 (0x0811)
CRC-16-IBM 	x16 + x15 + x2 + 1 (USB, many others; also known as "CRC-16") 	0x8005 or 0xA001 (0x4003)
CRC-24-Radix-64 	x24 + x23 + x18 + x17 + x14 + x11 + x10 + x7 + x6 + x5 + x4 + x3 + x + 1 	0x864CFB or 0xDF3261 (0xBE64C3)
CRC-32-Adler 	Not a CRC; see Adler-32 	See Adler-32
CRC-32-MPEG2 	x32 + x26 + x23 + x22 + x16 + x12 + x11 + x10 + x8 + x7 + x5 + x4 + x2 + x + 1 	0x04C11DB7 or 0xEDB88320 (0xDB710641) Also used in IEEE 802.3
CRC-32-IEEE 802.3 	x32 + x26 + x23 + x22 + x16 + x12 + x11 + x10 + x8 + x7 + x5 + x4 + x2 + x + 1 (V.42) 	0x04C11DB7 or 0xEDB88320 (0xDB710641)
CRC-32C (Castagnoli) 	x32 + x28 + x27 + x26 + x25 + x23 + x22 + x20 + x19 + x18 + x14 + x13 + x11 + x10 + x9 + x8 + x6 + 1 	0x1EDC6F41 or 0x82F63B78 (0x05EC76F1)
CRC-64-ISO 	x64 + x4 + x3 + x + 1 (use: ISO 3309) 	0x000000000000001B or 0xD800000000000000 (0xB000000000000001)
CRC-64-ECMA-182 	x64 + x62 + x57 + x55 + x54 + x53 + x52 + x47 + x46 + x45 + x40 + x39 + x38 + x37 + x35 + x33 + x32 + x31 + x29 + x27 + x24 + x23 + x22 + x21 + x19 + x17 + x13 + x12 + x10 + x9 + x7 + x4 + x + 1
(as described in ECMA-182 p.63) 	0x42F0E1EBA9EA3693 or 0xC96C5795D7870F42 (0x92D8AF2BAF0E1E85)

*)

(* revision history

hm		9.6.2007	rev 1.0		
	original version 

hm		11.9.2007	rev 1.1
	deleted unused variable i

*)
END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Logic\/Others' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK matrix
VAR_INPUT
	x1, x2, x3, x4, X5 : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR_INPUT CONSTANT
	Release : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	code : BYTE;
	TP : BOOL;
	y1: BOOL := TRUE;
	y2, y3, y4 : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR
	line : BYTE := 1;
	X : ARRAY[1..4] OF BYTE; (* scan line inputs *)
	L : ARRAY[1..4] OF BYTE; (* scan line status *)
	i: INT;
	temp: BYTE;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	11 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

MATRIX is a matrix keyboard encoder for 4 rows and up to 5 columns.
matrix can send a code while a key is pressed and it sends another code while a key is released when the setup variable 'release' is set to true.
the setup variable release is false the code is only sent when the key is pressed.
the output byte holds the 5 columns in the lowest bits 0..2  and the row number in bits 4..6, while bit 7 is true for a key pressed and false for a key released.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
TP := FALSE;
code := 0;

(* read scan lines *)
X[line].0 := X1;
X[line].1 := X2;
X[line].2 := X3;
X[line].3 := X4;
X[line].4 := X5;

(* compare for change *)
FOR i := 1 TO 4 DO
	IF X[i] <> L[i] THEN
		(* scan line information has changed code need to be found and generated *)
		temp := x[i] XOR L[i];
		IF temp.0 THEN
			code := 1;
			code.7 := X[i].0;
			L[i].0 := X[i].0;
		ELSIF temp.1 THEN
			code := 2;
			code.7 := X[i].1;
			L[i].1 := X[i].1;
		ELSIF temp.2 THEN
			code := 3;
			code.7 := X[i].2;
			L[i].2 := X[i].2;
		ELSIF temp.3 THEN
			code := 4;
			code.7 := X[i].3;
			L[i].3 := X[i].3;
		ELSIF temp.4 THEN
			code := 5;
			code.7 := X[i].4;
			L[i].4 := X[i].4;
		END_IF;
		i := 5;
		TP := TRUE;
		Code.4 := Line.0;
		Code.5 := Line.1;
		Code.6 := Line.2;

		(* check if release codes need to be killed *)
		IF NOT release AND code < 127 THEN
			code := 0;
			TP := 0;
		END_IF;
	END_IF;
END_FOR;

(* increment scan line every cycle *)
CASE line OF
	1 :	Line := 2;
		Y1 := FALSE; Y3 := FALSE; Y4 := FALSE; Y2 := TRUE;
	2 :	Line := 3;
		Y1 := FALSE; Y2 := FALSE; Y4 := FALSE; Y3 := TRUE;
	3 :	Line := 4;
		Y1 := FALSE; Y2 := FALSE; Y3 := FALSE; Y4 := TRUE;
	4 :	Line := 1;
		Y2 := FALSE; Y3 := FALSE; Y4 := FALSE; Y1 := TRUE;
END_CASE;

(* revision history
hm		10.6.2007	rev 1.0		
	original version 


hm		11.9.2007	rev 1.1		
	deleted unused variables k and old_code
*)

END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical\/array functions' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION _array_init : BOOL
VAR_INPUT
	pt : POINTER TO ARRAY[0..32000] OF REAL;
	size : INT;
	init : REAL;
END_VAR
VAR
	i: INT;
	stop: INT;
END_VAR


(*
version 1.1	6 jan 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function will initialize a given array with a value init.
the function needs to be called:	_array_init(adr("array"),sizeof("array"));
this function will manipulate a given array.
the function manipulates the original array, it rerturnes true when finished.
because this function works with pointers its very time efficient and it needs no extra memory.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
stop := (size - SIZEOF(pt)) / SIZEOF(pt);
FOR i := 0 TO stop DO
	pt^[i] := init;
END_FOR;
_array_init := TRUE;

(* revision History

hm 6.1.2007	rev 1.1
change type of function to bool
added  array_init := true to set output true.

*)
END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical\/array functions' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION _array_median : REAL
VAR_INPUT
	pt : POINTER TO ARRAY[0..32000] OF REAL;
	size : INT;
END_VAR
VAR
	i: INT;
	m: INT;
	temp : REAL;
	stop: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	3 mar 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function will calculate the median of a given array.
in order to do so the ariginal array is sorted and stays sorted after the function finishes
the function needs to be called:	_array_median(adr("array"),sizeof("array"));
this function will manipulate a given array.
the function will return the median of the original array.
for example [12,0,4,7,1] the median is 4 and the array after the function is called is [0,1,4,7,12]
because this function works with pointers its very time efficient and it needs no extra memory.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
stop := (size - SIZEOF(pt)) / SIZEOF(pt);
FOR i := 0 TO stop - 1 DO
	FOR m := i + 1 TO stop DO
		IF pt^[i] > pt^[m] THEN
			temp := pt^[i];
			pt^[i] := pt^[m];
			pt^[m] := temp;
		END_IF;
	END_FOR;
END_FOR;
IF even(stop) THEN
	_array_median := pt^[stop/2];
ELSE
	i := stop/2;
	_array_median := (pt^[i] + pt^[i+1])/2;
END_IF;

(* revision history
hm 3.3.2007	rev 1.1
	corrected an error, changed the statement line 14	i := TRUNC(stop/2); to i := stop/2;

*)
END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical\/array functions' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION _array_sort : BOOL
VAR_INPUT
	pt : POINTER TO ARRAY[0..32000] OF REAL;
	size : INT;
END_VAR
VAR
	i: INT;
	m: INT;
	temp : REAL;
	stop: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	6 jan 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function will sort a given array.
the function needs to be called:	_array_sort(adr("array"),sizeof("array"));
this function will manipulate a given array.
the function will not return anything except true, it will instead manipulate the original array.
because this function works with pointers its very time efficient and it needs no extra memory.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
stop := (size - SIZEOF(pt)) / SIZEOF(pt);
FOR i := 0 TO stop - 1 DO
	FOR m := i + 1 TO stop DO
		IF pt^[i] > pt^[m] THEN
			temp := pt^[i];
			pt^[i] := pt^[m];
			pt^[m] := temp;
		END_IF;
	END_FOR;
END_FOR;
_array_sort := TRUE;

(* revision history

hm 6.1.2007 	rev 1.1
	changed return value to true

*)
END_FUNCTION

	pt : POINTER TO ARRAY[0..32000] OF REAL;
	size : INT;
END_VAR

	i: INT;
	stop: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	2 oct 2006
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function will calculate the average of a given array.

array_avg := pt^[0];
FOR i := 1 TO stop DO
	array_avg := array_avg + pt^[i];
END_FOR;
array_avg := array_avg / (stop + 1);

END_FUNCTION

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical\/array functions' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION array_spr : REAL
VAR_INPUT
	pt : POINTER TO ARRAY[0..32000] OF REAL;
	size : INT;
END_VAR
VAR
	i: INT;
	stop: INT;
	array_max : REAL;
	array_min : REAL;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	2 oct 2006
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function will calculate the spread of a given array.
the function needs to be called:	array_spr(adr("array"),sizeof("array"));
for example: spread of [12,0,4,1,7] is 12 - 0 = 12.
because this function works with pointers its very time efficient and it needs no extra memory.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
stop := (size -SIZEOF(pt)) / SIZEOF(pt);
array_min := pt^[0];
array_max := pt^[0];
FOR i := 1 TO stop DO
	IF pt^[i] > array_max THEN array_max := pt^[i];
	ELSIF pt^[i] < array_min THEN array_min := pt^[i];
	END_IF;
END_FOR;
array_spr := array_max - array_min;

END_FUNCTION

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical\/array functions' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION array_trend : REAL
VAR_INPUT
	pt : POINTER TO ARRAY[0..32000] OF REAL;
	size : INT;
END_VAR
VAR
	i: INT;
	stop: INT;
	x: REAL;
	y : REAL;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	2 oct 2006
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function will calculate the trend of a given array.
trend will calculate the avg of the first half of the array and then the avg of the second half, trend = avg2 - avg1.
for example:  [0,1,4,5,3,4,6,3] = 4 - 2.5 = 1.5
the function needs to be called:	array_trend(adr("array"),sizeof("array"));
because this function works with pointers its very time efficient and it needs no extra memory.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
stop := (size - SIZEOF(pt)) / SIZEOF(pt);
FOR i := 0 TO stop / 2 DO x := x + pt^[i]; END_FOR;
X := x / (TRUNC(stop / 2) + 1);
IF even(stop) THEN
	FOR i := stop / 2 TO stop DO y := y + pt^[i]; END_FOR;
	y := y / (stop / 2 + 1);
ELSE
	FOR i := TRUNC(stop / 2) + 1 TO stop DO y := y + pt^[i]; END_FOR;
	y := y / (TRUNC(stop / 2) + 1);
END_IF;
array_trend := y - x;

END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical\/array functions' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION array_var : REAL
VAR_INPUT
	pt : POINTER TO ARRAY[0..32000] OF REAL;
	size : INT;
END_VAR
VAR
	avg : REAL;
	i: INT;
	stop: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	1 apr 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function will calculate the variance of a given array.
the function needs to be called:	array_var(adr("array"),sizeof("array"));
because this function works with pointers its very time efficient and it needs no extra memory.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* at first we calualte the arithmetic average of the array *)

stop := (size -SIZEOF(pt)) / SIZEOF(pt);
avg := pt^[0];
FOR i := 1 TO stop DO
	avg := avg + pt^[i];
END_FOR;
avg := avg / (stop + 1);

(* in a second run we calculate the variance of the array *)

array_var := EXPT(pt^[0] - avg, 2);
FOR i := 1 TO stop DO
	array_var := array_var + EXPT(pt^[i] - avg, 2);
END_FOR;
array_var := array_var / stop;

(* revision history
hm 1.4.2007	rev 1.0
	function created
*)
END_FUNCTION

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical\/functions' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK FT_avg
VAR_INPUT
	in : REAL;
	en : BOOL;
	N : INT;
	rst : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	avg : REAL;
END_VAR
VAR
	buff : delay;
	i: INT;
	init : BOOL;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	7 jan 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function calculates the average over n samples from a sequential input
the input values are shifted into an N deep buffer and the avg of this buffer is diplayed at anytime on the output.
a rst will load the buffer with the current in value..

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* limit n to a max of 32 because delay can do max 32 cycles *)
IF N > 32 THEN
	buff.n := 32;
ELSIF N < 0 THEN
	Buff.n := 0;
ELSE
	buff.n := N;
END_IF;

IF NOT init THEN
	FOR i := 1 TO N DO
		buff(in := in);
	END_FOR;
	avg := in;
	init := TRUE;
ELSIF rst THEN
	FOR i := 1 TO N DO
		buff(in := in);
	END_FOR;
	avg := in;
ELSIF en THEN
	buff(in := in);
	avg := avg + (in - buff.out)/N;
END_IF;

(* revision history

hm	7.1.2007	rev 1.1
	chaged rst logic to load the buffer with the actual input value instead of 0.
	added en input to allow better control of signal flow
	added init to load the buffer with in at startup to avoid rampup at beginning.
	deleted unused variable cnt.
*)
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical\/functions' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK FT_min_max
VAR_INPUT
	in : REAL;
	rst : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	mx : REAL;
	mn : REAL;
END_VAR
VAR
	init: BOOL;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	1 sep 2006
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function block stores the min and max value of an input signal.
when rst is true the mn and mx outputs are set to the in value.
when a rst is never active the function autoresets to the in value at startup.
since the input might not be present at first cycle the mn and mx are set during second cycle.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
IF rst OR NOT init THEN
	mn := in;
	mx := in;
	init := 1;
ELSIF in < mn THEN mn := in;
ELSIF in > mx THEN mx := in;
END_IF;
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical\/functions' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK FT_rmp
VAR_INPUT
	Rmp : BOOL := TRUE;
	in : REAL;
	KR : REAL;
	KF : REAL;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	out : REAL;
	busy : BOOL;
	UD : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR
	tx: TIME;
	last: TIME;
	init: BOOL;
END_VAR

(*
	version 1.3	17 sep 2007
	programmer 	oscat
	tested BY		oscat

this ramp function follows an input signal with a linear ramp up or down, the up or down speed can be set with KF and KR.
a K factor of 1 means 1 unit per second on the output. K factors can only be positive and not negative.
a busy output signals the ramp is running or busy false means the in value is present on the output.
a rmp input false means the output follows the input dierctly while a rmp = true means the output follows the input with a ramp.
a updn output signal the directon of the ramp (up or down).

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* read system time *)
tx := DWORD_TO_TIME(T_PLC_MS()) - last;

IF NOT init THEN
	init := TRUE;
	last := tx;
	tx := t#0s;
	out := in;
END_IF;
IF NOT rmp THEN
	out := in;
	busy := FALSE;
ELSIF out > in AND kf > 0 THEN
	(* ramp down *)
	out := out - TIME_TO_REAL(tx) / 1000 * KF;
	IF out < in THEN out := in; END_IF;
ELSIF out < in AND kr > 0 THEN
	(* ramp up *)
	out := out + TIME_TO_REAL(tx) / 1000 * KR;
	IF out > in THEN out := in; END_IF;
END_IF;

(* set busy and dir flags *)
IF out < in THEN
	busy := TRUE;
	ud := 1;
ELSIF out > in THEN
	busy := TRUE;
	ud := 0;
ELSE
	busy := FALSE;
END_IF;
last := last + tx;


(* revision history:

hm 8.10.2006			rev 1.1
	added ud output

hm 12. feb 2007		rev 1.2
	added init variable and corrected a possible startup problem

hm	17. sep 2007	rev 1.3
	replaced time() with t_plc_ms() for compatibility reasons

*)
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)

(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION asinH : REAL
VAR_INPUT
	X : REAL;
END_VAR
VAR

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION fact : INT
VAR_INPUT
	X : INT;
END_VAR
VAR
	i: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	4 mar 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function calculates the factorial of x
this simple factorial only calculates factorials for inputs up to 7
if the input is negative or higher then 7 the output will be -1.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
IF x >= 0 AND x < 8 THEN
	fact := 1;
	i := 1;
	WHILE i <= x DO
		fact := fact * i;
		i := i + 1;
	END_WHILE;
ELSE
	fact := -1;
END_IF;

(* revision history
hm 4.3.2007	rev 1.1
	changed a critical error where while loop was indefinite.

*)
END_FUNCTION

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION modR : REAL
VAR_INPUT
	in : REAL;
	divi : REAL;
END_VAR
VAR
END_VAR
VAR
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	4 aug 2006
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this is a modulo funtion for real numbers
modr(5.5,2.5) = 0.5


execution time on wago 750 - 841 =  29  us
*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
IF divi = 0 THEN
	modR := 0;
ELSE
	modR := in - TRUNC(in / divi)*divi;
END_IF;

(* revision history

hm 4.8.2006	rev 1.0

hm 28.1.2007	rev 1.1
	modr(x,0) will deliver the result 0

*)
END_FUNCTION

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/mathematical' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION RDM : REAL
VAR_INPUT
	last : REAL;
END_VAR
VAR
	temp: REAL;
END_VAR


(*
version 1.0	16 jan 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

this function calculates a pseudo random number
to generate the number it reads the sps timer and calculates a random number between 0 and 1:
in order to use rdm more then once within one sps cycle it need to be called with different seed numbers LAST.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
temp := TIME_TO_WORD(TIME());
RDM := fract(modR(temp*e, pi-last) + modR(temp*pi + last,e-last));

END_FUNCTION

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/other' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK ESR_collect
VAR_INPUT
	ESR_0, ESR_1, ESR_2, ESR_3, ESR_4, ESR_5, ESR_6, ESR_7 : ARRAY [0..3] OF esr_data;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	ESR_OUT : ARRAY[0..63] OF esr_data;
	pos : INT;
END_VAR
VAR CONSTANT
	max_in : INT := 3; (* maximum element of input variable *)
	max_out : INT := 63; (* maximum element of output array *)
END_VAR
VAR
	cnt : INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	26 jan 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

ESR_collect collects esr data from up to 8 esr_mon modules and stroes them in an output array.
the output pos will display the position of the last element in the array.
if the array will be full, the oldest element is overwritten.

*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
FOR cnt := 0 TO max_in DO
	IF esr_0[cnt].typ > 0 THEN
		esr_out[pos] := esr_0[cnt];
		pos := pos + 1;
		IF pos > max_out THEN pos := 0; END_IF;
	END_IF;
END_FOR;
FOR cnt := 0 TO max_in DO
	IF esr_1[cnt].typ > 0 THEN
		esr_out[pos] := esr_1[cnt];
		pos := pos + 1;
		IF pos > max_out THEN pos := 0; END_IF;
	END_IF;
END_FOR;
FOR cnt := 0 TO max_in DO
	IF esr_2[cnt].typ > 0 THEN
		esr_out[pos] := esr_2[cnt];
		pos := pos + 1;
		IF pos > max_out THEN pos := 0; END_IF;
	END_IF;
END_FOR;
FOR cnt := 0 TO max_in DO
	IF esr_3[cnt].typ > 0 THEN
		esr_out[pos] := esr_3[cnt];
		pos := pos + 1;
		IF pos > max_out THEN pos := 0; END_IF;
	END_IF;
END_FOR;
FOR cnt := 0 TO max_in DO
	IF esr_4[cnt].typ > 0 THEN
		esr_out[pos] := esr_4[cnt];
		pos := pos + 1;
		IF pos > max_out THEN pos := 0; END_IF;
	END_IF;
END_FOR;
FOR cnt := 0 TO max_in DO
	IF esr_5[cnt].typ > 0 THEN
		esr_out[pos] := esr_5[cnt];
		pos := pos + 1;
		IF pos > max_out THEN pos := 0; END_IF;
	END_IF;
END_FOR;
FOR cnt := 0 TO max_in DO
	IF esr_6[cnt].typ > 0 THEN
		esr_out[pos] := esr_6[cnt];
		pos := pos + 1;
		IF pos > max_out THEN pos := 0; END_IF;
	END_IF;
END_FOR;
FOR cnt := 0 TO max_in DO
	IF esr_7[cnt].typ > 0 THEN
		esr_out[pos] := esr_7[cnt];
		pos := pos + 1;
		IF pos > max_out THEN pos := 0; END_IF;
	END_IF;
END_FOR;
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/other' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK ESR_MON_B8
VAR_INPUT
	s0, s1, s2, s3, s4, s5, s6, s7 : BOOL;
	DT_in : DT;
END_VAR
VAR_INPUT CONSTANT
	a0, a1, a2, a3, a4, a5, a6, a7 : STRING(10);
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	ESR_Out: ARRAY [0..3] OF esr_data;
	ESR_Flag : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR
	x0, x1, x2, x3, x4, x5, x6, x7 : BOOL;
	tx: TIME;
	cnt : INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	17 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

ESR_mon_B8 monitores up to 8 binary inputs and reports changes with time stamd and adress label.
the module checks 8 inputs for a change and reports all changes with time and adress stamp to the output.
4 events maximum can be collected at once within the same cycle

*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* read system timer *)
tx := DWORD_TO_TIME(T_PLC_MS());

ESR_Flag := FALSE;
esr_out[3].typ := 0;
esr_out[2].typ := 0;
esr_out[1].typ := 0;
esr_out[0].typ := 0;
cnt := 0;

(* check if inputs have chaged and fill buffer *)
IF s0 <> X0 THEN
	IF s0 THEN esr_out[cnt].typ := 11; ELSE 	esr_out[cnt].typ := 10; END_IF;
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a0;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	X0 := S0;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF s1 <> X1 THEN
	IF s1 THEN esr_out[cnt].typ := 11; ELSE 	esr_out[cnt].typ := 10; END_IF;
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a1;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	X1 := S1;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF s2 <> X2 THEN
	IF s2 THEN esr_out[cnt].typ := 11; ELSE 	esr_out[cnt].typ := 10; END_IF;
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a2;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	X2 := S2;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF s3 <> X3 THEN
	IF s3 THEN esr_out[cnt].typ := 11; ELSE 	esr_out[cnt].typ := 10; END_IF;
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a3;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	X3 := S3;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF s4 <> X4 AND cnt < 4 THEN
	IF s4 THEN esr_out[cnt].typ := 11; ELSE 	esr_out[cnt].typ := 10; END_IF;
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a4;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	X4 := S4;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF s5 <> X5  AND cnt < 4 THEN
	IF s5 THEN esr_out[cnt].typ := 11; ELSE 	esr_out[cnt].typ := 10; END_IF;
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a5;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	X5 := S5;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF s6 <> X6  AND cnt < 4 THEN
	IF s6 THEN esr_out[cnt].typ := 11; ELSE 	esr_out[cnt].typ := 10; END_IF;
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a6;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	X6 := S6;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF s7 <> X7  AND cnt < 4 THEN
	IF s7 THEN esr_out[cnt].typ := 11; ELSE 	esr_out[cnt].typ := 10; END_IF;
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a7;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	X7 := S7;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;

(* revision history
hm	26. jan 2007		rev 1.0
	original version

hm	17. sep 2007	rev 1.1
	replaced time() with T_PLC_MS() for compatibility reasons
	
*)
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/other' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK ESR_MON_R4
VAR_INPUT
	R0, R1, R2, R3 : REAL;
	DT_in : DT;
END_VAR
VAR_INPUT CONSTANT
	a0, a1, a2, a3 : STRING(10);
	s0, s1, s2, s3 : REAL;
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	ESR_Out: ARRAY [0..3] OF esr_data;
	ESR_Flag : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR
	x0, x1, x2, x3 : REAL;
	tx: TIME;
	cnt : INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1 17 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

ESR_mon_R4 monitores up to 4 Real inputs and reports changes with time stamd and adress label.
the module checks 4 inputs for a change of more than the specified sensitivity S and reports all changes with time and adress stamp to the output.

*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* read system timer *)
tx := DWORD_TO_TIME(T_PLC_MS());

ESR_Flag := FALSE;
esr_out[3].typ := 0;
esr_out[2].typ := 0;
esr_out[1].typ := 0;
esr_out[0].typ := 0;
cnt := 0;

(* check if inputs have chaged and fill buffer *)
IF differ(R0,  X0, S0) THEN
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a0;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	esr_out[cnt].data[0] := REAL_TO_BYTE(R0);
	esr_out[cnt].data[1] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R0),8));
	esr_out[cnt].data[2] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R0),16));
	esr_out[cnt].data[3] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R0),24));
	X0 := R0;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF differ(R1,  X1, S1) THEN
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a1;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	esr_out[cnt].data[0] := REAL_TO_BYTE(R1);
	esr_out[cnt].data[1] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R1),8));
	esr_out[cnt].data[2] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R1),16));
	esr_out[cnt].data[3] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R1),24));
	X1 := R1;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF differ(R2,  X2, S2) THEN
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a2;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	esr_out[cnt].data[0] := REAL_TO_BYTE(R2);
	esr_out[cnt].data[1] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R2),8));
	esr_out[cnt].data[2] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R2),16));
	esr_out[cnt].data[3] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R2),24));
	X2 := R2;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF differ(R3,  X3, S3) THEN
	esr_out[cnt].adress := a3;
	esr_out[cnt].DS := DT_in;
	esr_out[cnt].TS := TX;
	esr_out[cnt].data[0] := REAL_TO_BYTE(R3);
	esr_out[cnt].data[1] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R3),8));
	esr_out[cnt].data[2] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R3),16));
	esr_out[cnt].data[3] := DWORD_TO_BYTE(SHR(REAL_TO_DWORD(R3),24));
	X3 := R3;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;


(* revision history
hm	26. jan 2007		rev 1.0
	original version

hm	17. sep 2007	rev 1.1
	replaced time() with T_PLC_MS() for compatibility reasons
	
*)

END_FUNCTION_BLOCK


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/other' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION_BLOCK ESR_MON_X8
VAR_INPUT
	s0, s1, s2, s3, s4, s5, s6, s7 : BYTE;
	DT_in : DT;
	Mode : BYTE := 3;
END_VAR
VAR_INPUT CONSTANT
	a0, a1, a2, a3, a4, a5, a6, a7 : STRING(10);
END_VAR
VAR_OUTPUT
	ESR_Out: ARRAY [0..3] OF esr_data;
	ESR_Flag : BOOL;
END_VAR
VAR
	x0, x1, x2, x3, x4, x5, x6, x7 : BYTE;
	tx: TIME;
	cnt : INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	17 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

ESR_MON_X8 is a status and error collector.
the module checks 8 status inputs for a change and reports up to 4 input changes with time and adress stamp to the output.
the mode can be 
1 for error only
2 for error and status
3 for error, status and debug
the adress label of the 8 inputs can be configured individually.
*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* read system timer *)
tx := DWORD_TO_TIME(T_PLC_MS());

ESR_Flag := FALSE;
esr_out[3].typ := 0;
esr_out[2].typ := 0;
esr_out[1].typ := 0;
esr_out[0].typ := 0;
cnt := 0;

(* check if inputs have chaged and fill buffer *)
IF s0 <> X0 AND ((s0 < 100) OR (S0 > 99 AND S0 < 200 AND mode >= 2) OR (S0 > 199 AND mode = 3)) THEN
	esr_out[cnt] := status_to_ESR(s0, a0, DT_in, TX);
	X0 := S0;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF s1 <> X1 AND ((s1 < 100) OR (S1 > 99 AND S1 < 200 AND mode >= 2) OR (S1 > 199 AND mode = 3)) THEN
	esr_out[cnt] := status_to_ESR(s1, a1, DT_in, TX);
	X1 := S1;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF s2 <> X2 AND ((s2 < 100) OR (S2 > 99 AND S2 < 200 AND mode >= 2) OR (S2 > 199 AND mode = 3)) THEN
	esr_out[cnt] := status_to_ESR(s2, a2, DT_in, TX);
	X2 := S2;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF s3 <> X3 AND ((s3 < 100) OR (S3 > 99 AND S3 < 200 AND mode >= 2) OR (S3 > 199 AND mode = 3)) THEN
	esr_out[cnt] := status_to_ESR(s3, a3, DT_in, TX);
	X3 := S3;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF cnt < 4 AND s4 <> X4 AND ((s4 < 100) OR (S4 > 99 AND S4 < 200 AND mode >= 2) OR (S4 > 199 AND mode = 3)) THEN
	esr_out[cnt] := status_to_ESR(s4, a4, DT_in, TX);
	X4 := S4;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF cnt < 4 AND s5 <> X5 AND ((s5 < 100) OR (S5 > 99 AND S5 < 200 AND mode >= 2) OR (S5 > 199 AND mode = 3)) THEN
	esr_out[cnt] := status_to_ESR(s5, a5, DT_in, TX);
	X5 := S5;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF cnt < 4 AND s6 <> X6 AND ((s6 < 100) OR (S6 > 99 AND S6 < 200 AND mode >= 2) OR (S6 > 199 AND mode = 3)) THEN
	esr_out[cnt] := status_to_ESR(s6, a6, DT_in, TX);
	X6 := S6;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;
IF cnt < 4 AND s7 <> X7 AND ((s7 < 100) OR (S7 > 99 AND S7 < 200 AND mode >= 2) OR (S7 > 199 AND mode = 3)) THEN
	esr_out[cnt] := status_to_ESR(s7, a7, DT_in, TX);
	X7 := S7;
	cnt := cnt + 1;
	esr_flag := TRUE;
END_IF;


(* revision history
hm	26. jan 2007		rev 1.0
	original version

hm	17. sep 2007	rev 1.1
	replaced time() with T_PLC_MS() for compatibility reasons
	
*)
END_FUNCTION_BLOCK

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION BYTE_TO_STRB : STRING
VAR_INPUT
	IN : BYTE;
END_VAR
VAR
	i: INT;
	temp : STRING;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	9 jun 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

BYTE_TO_STRINGB converts a Byte to a String of Bits represented by '0' and '1' s.
The lowest order bit will be on the right and the high order bit on the left.

*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
FOR i := 1 TO 8 DO
	IF in.0 = 0 THEN temp := CONCAT('0', temp); ELSE temp := CONCAT('1', temp); END_IF;
	in := SHR(in, 1);
END_FOR;
BYTE_TO_STRB := temp;

(* revision history

hm		9.6.2007	rev 1.0		original version 

*)
END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION BYTE_TO_STRH : STRING
VAR_INPUT
	IN : BYTE;
END_VAR
VAR
	i: INT;
	temp : STRING;
	Cx : STRING;
	X: BYTE;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	11 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

BYTE_TO_STRINGH converts a Byte to a String of Hexadecimal represented by '0' .. '9' and 'A' .. 'F'.
The lowest order Character will be on the right and the high order Character on the left.

*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
FOR i := 1 TO 2 DO
	X := in AND 2#1111;
	IF X <= 9 THEN X := X + 48; ELSE X := X + 55; END_IF;
	Cx := CHR(X);
	temp := CONCAT(Cx, temp);
	in := SHR(in,4);
END_FOR;
BYTE_TO_STRH := temp;

(* revision history

hm		9.6.2007		rev 1.0		
	original version 

hm		11.9.2007		rev 1.1		
	changed coding for compatibility with twincat, under twincat concat cannot have a function as argument.	

*)
END_FUNCTION

	C : BYTE;

	PT : POINTER TO BYTE;
END_VAR

(*

programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

CHR creates a character from a byte input and stuffs it in a one character length string.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
PT := ADR(CHR);
PT^ := C;

END_FUNCTION

FUNCTION DWORD_TO_STRB : STRING
VAR_INPUT
	IN : DWORD;
END_VAR
VAR
	i: INT;
	temp : STRING;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	9 jun 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

DWORD_TO_STRINGB converts a DWORD to a String of Bits represented by '0' and '1' s.
The lowest order bit will be on the right and the high order bit on the left.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
FOR i := 1 TO 32 DO
	IF in.0 THEN temp := CONCAT('1', temp); ELSE temp := CONCAT('0', temp); END_IF;
	in := SHR(in, 1);
END_FOR;
DWORD_TO_STRB := temp;

(* revision history

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION DWORD_To_STRF : STRING
VAR_INPUT
	IN : DWORD;
	N : INT;
END_VAR
VAR
	L: INT;
	temp: STRING;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	26 jan 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

dword_to_strF converts a DWORD, BYTE or Word to a fixed length String.
the string will be filles with leading zeroes to achieve the fixed length, or if too long, the lowest digits will be used.

for example:	dword_to_strf(123,4) = '0123' 
				dword_to_strf(123,2) = '23'
*)


(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* convert dword to string first and cut to length N *)
temp := RIGHT(DWORD_TO_STRING(in),N);
L := LEN(temp);
WHILE L < N DO
	temp := CONCAT('0', temp);
	L := L + 1;
END_WHILE;
DWORD_To_STRF := temp;
END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION DWORD_TO_STRH : STRING
VAR_INPUT
	IN : DWORD;
END_VAR

	i: INT;
	Cx : STRING;
	temp : STRING;
	X: BYTE;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	11 sep 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

DWORD_TO_STRINGH converts a DWORD to a String of Hexadecimal represented by '0' .. '9' and 'A' .. 'F'.
The lowest order Character will be on the right and the high order Character on the left.

*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
FOR i := 1 TO 8 DO
	X := DWORD_TO_BYTE(in AND 2#1111);
	IF X <= 9 THEN X := X + 48; ELSE X := X + 55; END_IF;
	Cx := CHR(X);
	temp := CONCAT(Cx, temp);
	in := SHR(in,4);
END_FOR;
DWORD_TO_STRH := temp;

(* revision history

		original version 

hm		11.9.2007		rev 1.1
		changed coding for compatibility with twincat, concat cannot support a function as an argument.
*)
END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION exec : STRING
VAR_INPUT
	str : STRING;
END_VAR
VAR
	pos: INT;
	R1: REAL;
	R2: REAL;
	operator: STRING;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	6 feb 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

exec executes a mathematical term and returns the result as a string
the term can only be a simple term without brackets and only one operator
allowed operastors are: (+, -, *, /, ^, sqrt, sin, cos, tan).

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
(* extract both numbers and operator *)
exec := uppercase(trim(str));

pos := findB_nonum(exec);
IF pos > 1 THEN R1 := STRING_TO_REAL(exec); END_IF;
R2 := STRING_TO_REAL(RIGHT(exec,LEN(exec)-pos));
exec := LEFT(exec,pos);
pos := findB_Num(exec);
operator := RIGHT(exec,LEN(exec) - pos);
IF operator = '' AND LEN(str) = 0 THEN
	exec := '';
	RETURN;
ELSIF operator = '' THEN
	exec := str;
	RETURN;
END_IF;
IF operator = '^' THEN
	exec := REAL_TO_STRING(EXPT(R1, R2));
ELSIF operator = 'SQRT' THEN
	exec := REAL_TO_STRING(SQRT(R2));
ELSIF operator = 'SIN' THEN
	exec := REAL_TO_STRING(SIN(r2));
ELSIF operator = 'COS' THEN
	exec := REAL_TO_STRING(COS(r2));
ELSIF operator = 'TAN' THEN
	exec := REAL_TO_STRING(TAN(R2));
ELSIF operator = '*' THEN
	exec := REAL_TO_STRING(R1 * R2);
ELSIF operator = '/' THEN
	IF R2 <> 0 THEN exec := REAL_TO_STRING(R1 / R2); ELSE exec := 'ERROR'; END_IF;
ELSIF operator = '+' THEN
	exec := REAL_TO_STRING(r1 + r2);
ELSIF operator = '-' THEN
	exec := REAL_TO_STRING(r1 - r2);
ELSE
	exec := 'ERROR';
END_IF;


(* revision history

hm 6.feb 2007	rev 1.1
	cos has to be written in uppercase
	divide by 0 will return an error
     
*)
END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION find_nonum : INT
VAR_INPUT
	str : STRING;
END_VAR
VAR
	pos: INT;
	pt : POINTER TO BYTE;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	6 oct 2006
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

find_noNum searches str and returns the first position which is not a number.
a number is characterized by a letter "0..9" or "."

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
pt := ADR(str);
find_nonum := 0;
FOR pos := 1 TO LEN(str) DO;
	IF NOT((PT^ > 47 AND PT^ < 58) OR PT^ = 46) THEN
		find_nonum := pos;
		RETURN;
	END_IF;
	PT := PT + 1;
END_FOR;

END_FUNCTION

	IF (PT^ > 47 AND PT^ < 58) OR PT^ = 46 THEN
		find_Num := pos;

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION FindB : INT
VAR_INPUT
	str1 : STRING;
	str2 : STRING;
END_VAR
VAR
	pos: INT;
	size: INT;
	length: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	6 oct 2006
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

the function find searches an str1 for the presence of str2 and returns the first position of str1 of the last presence in instring.
the function is similar to find except it searches from the right to left.
 a 0 is returned if the string is not found.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
size := LEN(str1);
length := LEN(str2);
FOR pos := size TO 1 BY -1 DO
	IF MID(str1,length,pos) = str2 THEN
		FindB := pos;
		RETURN;
	END_IF;
END_FOR;
END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)

	pos: INT;
	pt : POINTER TO BYTE;

findB_noNum searches str backwards and returns the last position which is not a number.
a number is characterized by a letter "0..9" or "."

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
pt := ADR(str) + LEN(str) - 1;
findB_nonum := 0;

	IF NOT((PT^ > 47 AND PT^ < 58) OR PT^ = 46) THEN
		findB_nonum := pos;
		RETURN;
	END_IF;
	PT := PT - 1;
END_FOR;

END_FUNCTION

FUNCTION lowercase : STRING

	str : STRING;
END_VAR

	PT : POINTER TO BYTE;
	pos: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	6 oct 2006

uppercase returns str while all letters A..Z are converted to lowercase.
*)

PT := ADR(lowercase);

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION Real_To_StrF : STRING
VAR_INPUT
	IN : REAL;
	N : INT;
END_VAR
VAR
	dw1 : DWORD;
	dw2 : DWORD;
	s1: STRING;
	s2 : STRING;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	26 jan 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

Real_to_strF converts a Real to a fixed length String.
the string will be filles with leading zeroes to achieve the fixed length, or if too long, the lowest digits will be used.


*)


(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
dw1 := TRUNC(ABS(in));
dw2 := TRUNC(round(fract(ABS(in))*EXPT(10,N),0));
IF in < 0 THEN
	s1 := CONCAT('-', DWORD_TO_STRING(dw1));
ELSE
	s1 := DWORD_TO_STRING(dw1);
END_IF;
	s1 := CONCAT(s1, '.');
s2 := DWORD_To_STRF(dw2,N);
Real_To_StrF := CONCAT(s1, s2);



END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION trim : STRING
VAR_INPUT
	str : STRING;
END_VAR
VAR
	pos: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	6 oct 2006
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

the function deletes all blanks within a string.

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
trim := str;
REPEAT
	pos := FIND(trim,' ');
	trim := REPLACE(trim,'',1,pos);
UNTIL pos = 0	END_REPEAT;

END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/String' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION uppercase : STRING
VAR_INPUT
	str : STRING;
END_VAR
VAR
	PT : POINTER TO BYTE;
	pos: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.0	6 oct 2006
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

uppercase returns str while all letters a..z are converted to uppercase

*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
PT := ADR(uppercase);
uppercase := str;
FOR pos := 1 TO LEN(str) DO
	IF PT^ > 96 AND PT^ < 123 THEN PT^ := PT^ - 32; END_IF;
	PT := PT + 1;
END_FOR;

END_FUNCTION


(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Time&Date' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION date_add : DATE
VAR_INPUT
	idate : DATE;
	D : INT;
	W : INT;
	M : INT;
	Y : INT;
END_VAR
VAR
	mo: INT;
	yr : INT;
END_VAR


(*
version 1.1	14 apr 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

date_add adds days, weeks, month or years to a date.
negative inputs are allowed for subtraction.

*)

(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
date_add := DWORD_TO_DATE(DATE_TO_DWORD(idate) + 86400 * d + 604800 * w);
yr := year(date_add) + y;
IF m > 0 THEN
	mo := month(date_add) + m;
	yr := yr + (mo - 1) / 12;
	mo := mo MOD 12;
	IF mo = 0 THEN mo := 12; END_IF;
	date_add := set_Date(yr, mo, day_of_month(date_add));
ELSIF m < 0 THEN
	mo := month(date_add) + m;
	yr := yr + mo / 12 -1;
	mo := mo MOD 12 + 12;
	date_add := set_Date(yr, mo, day_of_month(date_add));
ELSE
	date_add := set_Date(yr, month(date_add), day_of_month(date_add));
END_IF;

(* revision history

hm 27.12.2006	rev 1.0

hm 12.4.2007		rev 1.1
	corrected an error while date would be incorrect when year  = 0

*)
END_FUNCTION

(* @NESTEDCOMMENTS := 'Yes' *)
(* @PATH := '\/Time&Date' *)
(* @SYMFILEFLAGS := '2048' *)
FUNCTION day_of_month : INT
VAR_INPUT
	idate : DATE;
END_VAR
VAR
	yd: INT;
	yr: INT;
END_VAR

(*
version 1.1	22 Jan 2007
programmer 	hugo
tested by		tobias

returns the day OF month from any DATE
execution TIME with wago 750-841 = 65 us
*)
(* @END_DECLARATION := '0' *)
yr := DWORD_TO_INT((DATE_TO_DWORD(idate)/864+71954300)/36525);
yd := DWORD_TO_INT(DATE_TO_DWORD(idate)/86400 - TRUNC((yr-1)*365.25) + 719178);
IF yr MOD 4 = 0 THEN
	CASE yd OF
		1..31 	:	day_of_month := yd;
		32..60	:	day_of_month := yd - 31;
		61..91	:	day_of_month := yd - 60;
		92..121 :	day_of_month := yd - 91;
		122..152:	day_of_month := yd - 121;
		153..182:	day_of_month := yd - 152;
		183..213:	day_of_month := yd - 182;
		214..244:	day_of_month := yd - 213;
		245..274:	day_of_month := yd - 244;
		275..305:	day_of_month := yd - 274;
		306..335:	day_of_month := yd - 305;
		336..366:	day_of_month := yd - 335;
	END_CASE;
	ELSE
	CASE yd OF
		1..31 	:	day_of_month := yd;
		32..59	:	day_of_month := yd - 31;
		60..90	:	day_of_month := yd - 59;
		91..120 :	day_of_month := yd - 90;
		121..151:	day_of_month := yd - 120;
		152..181:	day_of_month := yd - 151;
		182..212:	day_of_month := yd - 181;
		213..243:	day_of_month := yd - 212;
		244..273:	day_of_month := yd - 243;
		274..304:	day_of_month := yd - 273;
		305..334:	day_of_month := yd - 304;
		335..365:	day_of_month := yd - 334;
	END_CASE;
	END_IF;




(*
this function is simple but took too long with 133 us
the problem is date_to_string is far too slow
